<div id="review_1367406995" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1367406995" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1367406995?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1367406995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9230479641685897340"><br/>Only last week I wrote that I don’t like to start multi-volume stories in progress, as I have neither the patience to wait years, nor the sharp memory to keep events and characters sorted out long term. But, what good are rules if you can’t make exceptions! Five years ago, my friends were all praising this new space opera thing by a new author: “The Expanse” by James S A Corey. When I learned that half of the creative team behind this alias is Daniel Abraham, I didn’t hesitate, and today I consi</span>
  <span id="freeText9230479641685897340" style="display:none"><br />Only last week I wrote that I don’t like to start multi-volume stories in progress, as I have neither the patience to wait years, nor the sharp memory to keep events and characters sorted out long term. But, what good are rules if you can’t make exceptions! Five years ago, my friends were all praising this new space opera thing by a new author: “The Expanse” by James S A Corey. When I learned that half of the creative team behind this alias is Daniel Abraham, I didn’t hesitate, and today I consider the series my summer blockbuster fix: disasters, special FX, larger than life characters, adventures, clever twists and cliffhanging endings that just force you to pick up the next one and find out how your heroes will survive this time. Of course, it helps that Abraham and Franck are churning out these novels like clockwork, never missing a deadline until now. It also helps that the quality is pretty consistent from one book to the next, making it very hard to pick a favorite episode.<br /><br />Actually, that remark about cliffhanger endings is only half true. There IS a jaw dropping event at the end of each installment, but the major plot of each book is self-contained, making it possible to start with the last one or in the middle of the series, if you somehow missed the start. The continuity for the five books already published is guaranteed by the crew of the space frigate “Rocinante” , a tightly knit freelance team under the leadership of captain Jim Holden. <br /><br />Jim, his girlfriend and second in command Naomi, his pilot Alex and his muscle-man gunner Amos have been through a lot together, and at the start of this episode, with the “Rocinante” severely damaged in the previous adventure, they are about to enjoy a well deserved vacation on an orbital station. Pretty soon though. Jim Holden discovers that his crew is not as tightly knit as he likes to think. Instead of waiting together for the reapirs to be finished, all three of his friends ask for special leave to take care of ‘personal’ business. Alex Kamal goes back to Mars, to try and patch things up with his ex. Amos Burton goes to Earth to pay homage to an old friend who passed away, and Naomi receives a secret summons from a ghost of her past. I thought initially that this scattering of the major POV characters all across the Solar System was only a clever plot maneuver to place them in key positions for the upcoming events, but there is a big bonus that turns the novel into my current favorite in the series. Namely, that it was about time we give ‘good guy’ Jim Holden a rest, and find out more about the people behind his hero image. <br /><br />While I enjoy the popcorn entertainment of the space opera, the real reason I rate the Expanse series so high is the talent of the authors to write engaging, believable characters. Holden is a great one, but he is painted mostly in shades of white: what you see is what you get, the burden of command, the idealist fighting for justice and all that jazz. Ambiguous, conflicted, secretive, evolving personalities are more my cup of tea, and with Amos, Alex and especially with the new revelations about Naomi I got a triple serving of my favorite dish. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ quintuple, if you count the two new additions to the Rocinante crew, Bobbie Draper the stormtrooper and Peaches the psychopatic killer. It was about time Naomi got some feminine help to even out the odds of the testosterone filled “Rocinante”  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I am deliberately not telling you anything about the big ‘Nemesis’ event, hoping you will get as big a shock as me when the time comes. I think it’s enough for now to say that even with the whole galaxy open for colonisation, there are still factions in the Solar System who nurse old grievances and have scores to settle. <br /><br /><i> The aliens that sent the protomolecule hadn’t needed to destroy humanity. They’d given the humans the opportunity to destroy themselves, and as a species, they’d leaped on it. </i><br /><br />When things go pear shaped, Amos, Alex and Naomi are suddenly unable to return to the orbital station and must find the inner strength and the resolve to survive without the usual support of their comrades and without the leadership of Jim Holden. But even absent from the action, the captain can still be an inspiration for his crew:<br /><br /><i> Even when the captain fucked up, he was acting in good faith. Amos hadn’t met many people like that. </i><br /><br />Amos is sorely in need of such a role model, as he gets closer to the Dark Side than any other crew member . Left to his own devices, he is best described as a psychopatic killer with a very short fuse. And what he’s going through down on Earth is enough to push over the edge even a saint. I bookmarked a short conversation between him and another reformed assassin, in the aftermath of a brutal beating:<br /><br /><i> Amos walked back toward the hangar. Sure enough, Peaches was standing in the doorway, her arms crossed. He wiped his hand. His knuckles were bleeding.<br />“See, that’s what civilization is,” he said. “Bunch of stories. That’s all.”<br />“So what if it is?” Peaches said. “We’re really good at telling stories. Everything just turned to shit, and we’re already finding ways to put it back together.” </i><br /><br />Which brings me to the third (or fourth) reason I love the series: no matter how dark things get, and they get sunk to the bottom of a dark hole in “Nemesis Games”, there’s always a chance to get up, dust yourself, and fight another day!<br /><br />All three storylines involving the ‘Rocinante’ crew members are dramatic and spectacular enough to warrant a spin-off movie or novel. Together they bring the house down, at least for me. Again, in trying to avoid spoilers, I can’t go into details, but I would like to see what others thought of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ a space jump between ships without a suit by Naomi. I personally don’t think it’s feasible, but I’m not a vacuum expert  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I know I am abusing the spoiler tags, but I am also curious about the hook at the end of the novel. Uncharacteristically, a lot of plot lines are left unresolved, and the overall status of the Solar System is a big mess. What will they come up with next?<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ It means I don’t own Medina Station, Fred said. It means that the most violent, hard-line, extremist faction of our group controls the choke point of the entire galaxy.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As an epitaph of sorts, and a reminder that we need a sense of humour to help get us over the rough spots, I will close my review with the heartfelt exclamation of one of the lead characters:<br /><br /><b> I think this has to qualify as the worst vacation ever. </b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9230479641685897340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1145918838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1145918838" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7022024-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470679918p2/7022024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1145918838?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7022024-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=here-be-aliens">here-be-aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=also-a-tv-show">also-a-tv-show</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1145918838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12656633154528312896">After the shortcomings of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/773720471?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>the previous installment</a>, I was a bit concerned that the shine might be off this delicious space opera apple (not a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956894845?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Star Carrier</a> level of concern, but still some). I was extremely happy to see my concerns obliterated and my faith in this series more than restored.<br/><br/>My biggest problem with the last book was that it felt very claustrophobic. I mean, the series is called <b>
  <i>Expanse</i>
</b>, but Cibola Burn mostly took place on one planet, nothing like the solar system (and beyond) </span>
  <span id="freeText12656633154528312896" style="display:none">After the shortcomings of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/773720471?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">the previous installment</a>, I was a bit concerned that the shine might be off this delicious space opera apple (not a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956894845?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Star Carrier</a> level of concern, but still some). I was extremely happy to see my concerns obliterated and my faith in this series more than restored.<br /><br />My biggest problem with the last book was that it felt very claustrophobic. I mean, the series is called <b>
  <i>Expanse</i>
</b>, but Cibola Burn mostly took place on one planet, nothing like the solar system (and beyond) spanning stories the first three books encompassed. Nemesis Games remedies this by "breaking up the band", sending Naomi, Alex, and Amos off to take care of some of their own business while their ship undergoes extensive repairs. This accomplishes two excellent things:<br /><br />1) Character development: another of my criticisms of Cibola Burn was the lack of character development. The main cast showed no change from the beginning of the book to the end. They were the kick ass good guys who kicked ass and did good. Sure it is entertaining, but it was not as rich in characterization as the previous installments. With Alex, Amos, and Naomi heading off to take care of some of their own business we get more of their backstory and their internal thought process. I thought this was particularly effective in Naomi's case. We already know her as an amazing engineer and independent woman but as we learn about her past (which very much informs contemporary events) and her battles with depression; she really becomes a much more fleshed out and deep character.<br /><br />2) Multiple Perspectives of Solar System Events: Nemesis Games returns us to events that span and affect the entire solar system. Instead of the POV characters all in one place reacting to the same information at the same time, each of the POV characters gets information at different times and have to overcome different challenges. It both shows each of their individuals strengths and highlights how important that they are to each other as a crew. The split of the crew also lets us to see some great characters from past books: Fred Johnson, Avasarala, and Bobbie. <br /><br />All in all the splitting of the crew and POV's really gave the story a much richer feel and context.<br /><br />Another great part of Nemesis Games was the antagonist. One of the underlying themes of this series is the tension between the planetary societies (Earth and Mars) and the Belters (people who live and operate in low gravity environments in the asteroid belt and moons). Before the series starts there is a history of Belters being exploited by Earth and Martian companies and governments. Lack of supplies, high fees/taxes, disregard for Belter welfare, etc. Generally a very tense relationship with extremists on both sides, but because both sides provides some benefits to the other a relationship worth preserving and improving...<br /><br />...At least until the opening of the gates to a thousand new worlds. Where certain minerals and substances came from the Belt, the new alien worlds offer an alternative and possible more stable/cheaper source of those substances. As such there is a large worry among Belters that they will simply be left behind as the rest of humanity expands to planets that, due to their adaptation for low gravity environments, Belters would be unable to take part in. Further, Belters have evolved into a unique society and identity independent of Earth and Martian origins. They see this exodus of humanity to the new worlds as a direct threat to their culture and way of life.<br /><br />Into this volatile mix, a group of Belter terrorist due some pretty terrible things in a terrifyingly effective and coordinated manner. I don't want to spoil much, but I will say the terrorists are scary competent and have a devastatingly effective plan to sow the seeds of chaos and destruction. And lurking in the background (as is the nature of Expanse books) is the protomolecule and some greater conspiracy that may just be using the Belter terrorists as a convenient tool for some greater plan that has yet to be revealed.<br /><br />The only slight, minor issue I had with the book was that this was more like the first half of a larger story. The conclusion leaves a lot of loose ends that need to be dealt with plus further mysteries about the gates themselves. But that does nothing to diminish this highly addictive and engaging read. Can't wait for the sixth book!<br /><br />And, because I guess it is something I do, some of my favorite passages form the book:<br /><br /><b>Yes, but think of the huge tracts of land</b>:<i>"But not all 1,300 systems have good surveys yet. Who knows what we'll find."<br /><br />"Killer robot things and continent sized fusion reactors just waiting for someone to flip the switch so they can blow half the planet into space, if memory serves." </i><br /><br /><b>Avasarla is still, literally, the best</b>: <i>"Either I'm not in any trouble or I am in all of it. How you doin', Chrissie?" <br /><br />"Good to see you too. Call me that again and I'll have an officer beat you gently with a cattle prod."</i><br /><br /><b>It is important to pace yourself, professionally speaking</b>:<i> "I made my name with the story on the Behemoth. Aliens and wormhole gates and a protomolecule ghost that only talked to the most famous person in the solar system. I don't think my follow-up to that can be "Humans Still Shitty to Each Other". Lacks panache."</i><br /><br /><b>James Holden's ancestors must have reproduced very quickly</b>:<i> "What did you do?" <br /><br />"There was a button. I pushed it."<br /><br />"Jesus Christ. That really is how you go through life, isn't it?" </i><br /><br /><b>I would watch the hell out of the Fred and Holden Show (as long as Avasarla guest starred)</b>:<i> "I've been trying to reach your hand terminal for the past fifteen minutes." <br /><br />"I may have left it in my pants. In my quarters. I think I did." <br /><br />"Are you drunk?" <br /><br />"I think I am." <br /><br />"And you're not wearing any pants?" <br /><br />"I'm not ready to take our relationship there yet."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12656633154528312896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1203586298" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1203586298" />
    <a title="Kevin Kelsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10445368-kevin-kelsey"><img alt="Kevin Kelsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588111734p2/10445368.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1203586298?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin Kelsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin Kelsey" href="/user/show/10445368-kevin-kelsey">Kevin Kelsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316334716" href="/book/show/26245068-nemesis-games">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445368-kevin-kelsey?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445368-kevin-kelsey?shelf=read-it-again">read-it-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10445368-kevin-kelsey?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1203586298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11801369942710186641">Easily the best in the series so far. No question about that. Instead of introducing several new characters and slowly weaving them into the plot along with the Rocinante crew, this one buckles down on the core characters and delivers in strides. A lot happens, considering that no time had to be spent giving us info on all new people, the bulk of the book fully develops backstories and gives us the goods on the main characters. <br/><br/>Naomi brings it all home in this one, and it's amazing to finally se</span>
  <span id="freeText11801369942710186641" style="display:none">Easily the best in the series so far. No question about that. Instead of introducing several new characters and slowly weaving them into the plot along with the Rocinante crew, this one buckles down on the core characters and delivers in strides. A lot happens, considering that no time had to be spent giving us info on all new people, the bulk of the book fully develops backstories and gives us the goods on the main characters. <br /><br />Naomi brings it all home in this one, and it's amazing to finally see her in action. She was always a little in the background in the previous books, but not here. The Amos chapters are pure fun, and his backstory first established in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20981355.The_Churn__The_Expanse___0_2_" title="The Churn (The Expanse, #0.2) by James S.A. Corey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Churn</a> is continued to a great conclusion. Bobbie is back, paired with Alex for most of the story, and Avasarala is as vulgar and pissed as ever. Her interactions with Amos were my favorite thing about this one.<br /><br />The story itself is a massive shakeup to this universe, and will have long lasting reverberations for the books to follow. Characters are changed, permanently. Big things happen. Stuff goes down. There was also some great setup for what's to follow. This book was complete in and of itself, but in a way it felt like the first half of an absolute epic. Book 6 is too far away right now, and I honestly feel like it's going to blow this whole series wide open for the remaining 3 books after.<br /><br />I am excited.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11801369942710186641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2555439928" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555439928" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2555439928?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781478933786" href="/book/show/41072926-nemesis-games">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2555439928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1504494816301163662">The first three books took place in our solar system, some time in the future. The fourth book switched to a more outwards look thanks to the ring gates and all the pathways they had opened. Since I'm a fan of stories about galactic discovery, I LOVED the new setting and all its possibilities. Alas, we are now back in Sol.<br/><br/>Part of me wanted to be out in the deep black and explore, see aliens or at least find more artifacts, connecting the dots, getting closer to solving the mystery of the builder</span>
  <span id="freeText1504494816301163662" style="display:none">The first three books took place in our solar system, some time in the future. The fourth book switched to a more outwards look thanks to the ring gates and all the pathways they had opened. Since I'm a fan of stories about galactic discovery, I LOVED the new setting and all its possibilities. Alas, we are now back in Sol.<br /><br />Part of me wanted to be out in the deep black and explore, see aliens or at least find more artifacts, connecting the dots, getting closer to solving the mystery of the builders.<br />Another part of me must admit that this story about the political turmoil that got started when the ring gates opened is realistic and still very interestingly executed. I mean, it would be utopic to think humanity would suddenly just get along because there are enough worlds out there for the individual factions so nobody would have to fight any longer. That would be the smart way to see it but since when have humans ever been this smart?<br />There is also the problem of the economies collapsing (or threatening to) as well as the different governments trying hard not to be left behind by their own subjects. *lol*<br />I guess it therefore comes as no surprise that there is quite the struggle in Sol and that the authors wanted to highlight that, to give the reader a bit more introspection.<br /><br />Thus, the crew of the Roci are at Tyco station at the beginning, where the ship needs extensive repairs. In order to pass the time, they split up (what could possibly go wrong?) with Amos going to Earth, Alex to Mars and Naomi ... Holden stays behind with Fred Johnson and that awful reporter Monica.<br />However, the past that is slowing reeling Naomi back in is also threatening the entire system and soon shit really hits the fan.<br /><br />As such, this more narrow perspective of events also served as a more closer look at the characters themselves. A bit more flesh on their bones so to speak. More about their pasts (for those who've read the short stories as much as for those who haven't), setting the scene for the crew to grow both in character and numbers (yep, you heard that correctly).<br /><br />Some events here are truly heartbreaking, such as <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Earth becoming uninhabitable or Avasarala not knowing if her beloved husband survived <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but the authors managed to balance that heartbreak against some of the best dialogues I've ever read, mostly between Avasarala and Amos. Chrissy, you're the best. ;)<br /><br />I did not, however, connect with Naomi. *lol* If anything, this has confirmed what I think about her, namely that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she liked to play the Roci's conscience while herself being a complete idiot and not really a good person. I mean, the way she made her exit from Holden, threatening him like that, then sauntering back in at the end with THAT line ... to say nothing of the typical trope of being a teenage mom, only here being made much worse by having abandoned the kid to a psychotic and abusive father in order for herself to survive. And no, a difficult childhood is NOT sufficient enough an excuse because how many of us have had one and didn't end up like that <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>?!<br />Nothing new, really, and it's actually a good sign since it points to the authors sticking with how they built their characters instead of catering to the audience or making unrealistic changes.<br /><br />Anyway, this was not what I had expected and except from the one massive thing happening this was on a smaller scale event-wise, but it was still written impeccably and had me enjoy every minute that I sat on the edge of my seat. To say nothing of that epilogue! Way to hook the readers!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1504494816301163662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3484349819" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3484349819?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sud666" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sud666" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3484349819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10047475419592685636">The cosmic epic of The Expanse continues. While there are some similarities to Season 4 of the show (which was a combination of this book and the previous "Cibola Burn"), but this is a fra darker and much more complex story.<br/><br/>The crew of the Roci decides to do some individual missions. Amos heads back home to Baltimore for a funeral; Alex goes back to Mars to try to reconnect with his old life; Naomi stupidly decides to go "help" her son and Holden is stuck on the Roci trying to help Fred Johnson.</span>
  <span id="freeText10047475419592685636" style="display:none">The cosmic epic of The Expanse continues. While there are some similarities to Season 4 of the show (which was a combination of this book and the previous "Cibola Burn"), but this is a fra darker and much more complex story.<br /><br />The crew of the Roci decides to do some individual missions. Amos heads back home to Baltimore for a funeral; Alex goes back to Mars to try to reconnect with his old life; Naomi stupidly decides to go "help" her son and Holden is stuck on the Roci trying to help Fred Johnson.<br /><br />No more spoilers. Now while that part is going on-there are some major "meta" developments. For one thing, the opening of the gates has led to the decline in power for Earth and Mars and is devastating to the Belters. A rouge OPA branch launches a devastating attack on the Earth and the repercussions will be immense. The other "meta" is that on top of all these human problems- some THING is making ships disappear. The book ends on a huge cliff hanger.<br /><br />Great sci-fi and a fun story. Sadly I shall have to wait however long it takes for the next book. let's pray James S.A. Corey do not channel their inner-G.R.R. Martin.</span>

<div id="review_1216796134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1216796134" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreas O" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreas O" href="/user/show/21205393-andreas-o">Andreas O</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1216796134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8516416599668943579">Moving the pieces.<br/><br/>Unspecified spoilers ahead.<br/><br/>Excitement. Drama. Character. Vast, sweeping changes to the universe. The book has it all.<br/><br/>Still, at the end, little that was not started in this book is resolved. The implications are not expanded on. What should have been a momentous, earth shattering change has less impact than the Ilus incident in the last book. The book ends long before the story does. This is half a book pretending to be whole. A good half. But still only half. <br/><br/>Pieces are moved a</span>
  <span id="freeText8516416599668943579" style="display:none">Moving the pieces.<br /><br />Unspecified spoilers ahead.<br /><br />Excitement. Drama. Character. Vast, sweeping changes to the universe. The book has it all.<br /><br />Still, at the end, little that was not started in this book is resolved. The implications are not expanded on. What should have been a momentous, earth shattering change has less impact than the Ilus incident in the last book. The book ends long before the story does. This is half a book pretending to be whole. A good half. But still only half. <br /><br />Pieces are moved around the board. Beautifully, momentuously and with great excitement for the future. But for now they're just pieces being moved around the board. What should have been a thriller winds up being a tease. <br /><br />George R.R. Martin did not get away with merely moving pieces in his fifth book. What on Earth possessed S.A. Corey to try the same?</span>

<div id="review_1330447862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1330447862" />
    <a title="Mr. Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15984059-mr-matt"><img alt="Mr. Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401911574p2/15984059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1330447862?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mr. Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mr. Matt" href="/user/show/15984059-mr-matt">Mr. Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15984059-mr-matt?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330447862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12703826742151058498">After the resolution of Cibola Burn, I thought surely the series was due for somewhat of a step back. Nope. The Expanse delivers again! Holden, Burton, Nagata, Kamal, and all the rest are back ... and so is the tension that the author has managed to keep at a high pitch over five books. Impressive. <br/><br/>Holden and company return from New Terra and split up - each pursuing some personal, somewhat hidden agenda. The break up of the company leaves Holden morose and struggling. His crew had become his fa</span>
  <span id="freeText12703826742151058498" style="display:none">After the resolution of Cibola Burn, I thought surely the series was due for somewhat of a step back. Nope. The Expanse delivers again! Holden, Burton, Nagata, Kamal, and all the rest are back ... and so is the tension that the author has managed to keep at a high pitch over five books. Impressive. <br /><br />Holden and company return from New Terra and split up - each pursuing some personal, somewhat hidden agenda. The break up of the company leaves Holden morose and struggling. His crew had become his family, and he misses them - all of them. As a reader, I appreciated the break up as it allowed for character development. The crew sometimes felt as if they were part of the background when compared to Holden's monopolization of the lime light. Now, we get to learn the backstories of Nagata, Burton and Kamal. <br /><br />Of course, it wouldn't be the Expanse if we weren't learning about those backstories in the midst of all hell breaking loose. A rogue force is working in the shadows to destabilize the existing power structure. Holden and his crew once again manages to find himself at the center of things, but it was nice that it wasn't all about Holden. For a change he is in the background. My two favorite narratives in this volume were Burton's and Nagata's.<br /><br />The crisis itself is well done. Without revealing more it is something that generates a strong reaction. I genuinely didn't see it coming, but when the first hit happened, I instantly knew what was afoot. And despite the fact that the crisis at first seems straight forward, I appreciate the fact that their is still, lurking in the shadows questions and hints of darker motives. Plots within plots. I like that.<br /><br />Four and a half stars rounded up to five. My only wish is that I want the author to get to the point. I'm worried that I am looking at a Wheel of Time series here - one that just never ends. Given where the story is at the end of book five, I struggle to understand how it can be wrapped up quickly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12703826742151058498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3146617963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3146617963" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53587416-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571965612p2/53587416.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3146617963?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/53587416-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3146617963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13032821856771637493">Frequently wistful and sometimes maudlin, as the Roci is stripped down for repair and the crew leaves Holden temporarily, going their separate ways to catch up on personal business. The first half has some deeply personal back stories on Naomi, Amos and Alex, each back on his/her home turf after a long absence and pondering the meaning and value of family, both old and new. Mars Marine Bobbie Draper and Clarissa "Peaches" Mao also play large roles, both great characters making a most welcome ret</span>
  <span id="freeText13032821856771637493" style="display:none">Frequently wistful and sometimes maudlin, as the Roci is stripped down for repair and the crew leaves Holden temporarily, going their separate ways to catch up on personal business. The first half has some deeply personal back stories on Naomi, Amos and Alex, each back on his/her home turf after a long absence and pondering the meaning and value of family, both old and new. Mars Marine Bobbie Draper and Clarissa "Peaches" Mao also play large roles, both great characters making a most welcome return. The tension and excitement pick up considerably in the second half as multiple, massive crises come to a head, testing loyalties to crew, family and country. What amazes me is how this series re-invents itself in completely unexpected ways. Just when you think it's going to zig, it zags from out of nowhere. Can't wait for the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13032821856771637493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1301785869" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301785869" />
    <a title="Raja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269927-raja"><img alt="Raja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586609384p2/269927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1301785869?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raja" href="/user/show/269927-raja">Raja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269927-raja?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269927-raja?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1301785869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8343991953240837777">The entire book is great... except for anything that has anything to do with one particular character. But first, the good: We're back to big spaces and high stakes, which is enjoyable after the sometimes claustrophobic fourth book in the series. It's more my speed. My favourite characters return, which is also pretty great. The earth-shattering events are handled deftly, and we see enough characters react to them that you can probably find your likely response in there somewhere. The ending, as</span>
  <span id="freeText8343991953240837777" style="display:none">The entire book is great... except for anything that has anything to do with one particular character. But first, the good: We're back to big spaces and high stakes, which is enjoyable after the sometimes claustrophobic fourth book in the series. It's more my speed. My favourite characters return, which is also pretty great. The earth-shattering events are handled deftly, and we see enough characters react to them that you can probably find your likely response in there somewhere. The ending, as usual, ties things up neatly while leaving hooks for the next book. <br /><br />MAJOR SPOILERS FROM HERE ON IN. <br /><br />NO, SERIOUSLY. HUGE SPOILERS. <br /><br />Frustration #1: Naomi's ex is Space Hitler. <br /><br />Frustration #2: Naomi has now spent two books in a row being a prisoner. <br /><br />I'll elaborate on those a little. <br /><br />(Side note: I can't believe that 1) the word "genocide" doesn't appear in the book, and 2) no one mentions Hitler, even when Fred is describing what he knows about Marco and more or less describes Hitler.)<br /><br />More importantly, though, Naomi's characterization in this book is approximately one hundred percent defined by how she relates to male characters. Marco says she needs to go help her son and she abandons everything; Marco lays a trap to kill Jim and she moves heaven and earth to stop it. <br /><br />I'd hoped that Naomi's deep dark secret would be something unrelated to her gender or past relationships. "I was a terrorist" is a great dark secret. "My ex is Space Hitler and he can still manipulate me into doing stuff" doesn't add to the first secret; I think it actually detracts. <br /><br />On the plus side, Naomi is intelligent and resorceful, and in both cases of book-length imprisonment she escapes on her own rather than being rescued. But for me, that wasn't enough to overcome my issues with the rest of her arc in the book. <br /><br />Hopefully, though, we're past that now and can carry on with the good stuff. Only four books left, so I'm expecting the alien revelations to start flowing a little faster now. Yes, Earth got blown up. But let's not put too fine a point on it: that was GENocide, and we know the things that perpetrated the XENocide of the protomolecule creators are still out there. The stakes are a lot bigger than Earth. <br /><br />Some spoilery good stuff: Everything involving Amos was awesome. Alex was also pretty great in this one. Bobbie was spectacular, Avasarala was her usual wonderful avuncular self. Watching Jim and Fred bounce off each other was also good. And, you know, spaceships. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8343991953240837777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2208857430" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2208857430" />
    <a title="Cathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/978552-cathy"><img alt="Cathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604572841p2/978552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2208857430?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy" href="/user/show/978552-cathy">Cathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25649238-nemesis-games">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2208857430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15752779594378568381">Fabulous. I think I have a new favourite in the Expanse series! 5 stars with a cherry on top. Some slight spoilers ahead...<br/><br/>All about Holden, Naomi, Alex and Amos, instead of the usual introduction of a new host of characters never to be seen again. <br/><br/>And Bobby is back! And Avasarala, potty-mouth and all.<br/><br/>This is like pure gold for the fans of the series. No distractions of getting to know other characters or slowly diving into a complicated storyline. Just our favourite crew, with their odd-ball hu</span>
  <span id="freeText15752779594378568381" style="display:none">Fabulous. I think I have a new favourite in the Expanse series! 5 stars with a cherry on top. Some slight spoilers ahead...<br /><br />All about Holden, Naomi, Alex and Amos, instead of the usual introduction of a new host of characters never to be seen again. <br /><br />And Bobby is back! And Avasarala, potty-mouth and all.<br /><br />This is like pure gold for the fans of the series. No distractions of getting to know other characters or slowly diving into a complicated storyline. Just our favourite crew, with their odd-ball humour, trying to survive against mounting odds in a pretty straight forward action adventure story. Don't get me wrong, the other books with their conspiracies, aliens, universe-spanning plots and amazing world building were fun, too. But this was a great joy ride in its straight forwardness and relative simplicity. And the action, twists and turns kept coming right from the start. I wanted to take breaks between chapters, but I just couldn't, I was having too much fun...<br /><br />My favourite stories were those of Amos and Naomi. Holden's was fun, too, but more of a filler. Alex's story interested me the least. Each of those plots easily could have been the basis for full novels of their own. <br /><br />Waiting till next month for my fellow buddy readers to pick up the next book of the series is going to be hard...<br /><br />*~*~*~*<br />P.S.: Reading the short story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2208868058?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Churn</a> beforehand is recommended, it gives background on Amos Burton's youth and characters that are relevant to this story arc.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15752779594378568381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ePWL1MXX8RUrfCYddoaWOtcuGSNFSamO4NWyywgqkFYQsgWREzijFrJa1BvZrv4UEPBA3aMPH5Jcx03l+L/+mQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5Pye30O3Fkk2l4pQzUBfXwDtEBjwh/JLHhY7eBeqbCCMuxCalVhESq+xeFZiaDdxxzNJ5hbBRFeiBMRW5z8C7w==')})
  }
